<div id="review_218910759" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/218910759" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5903843-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603562140p2/5903843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/218910759?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/5903843-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903843-matt?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer218910759" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6320412401876384851">What do you get when you mix the forensic description of Kathy Reichs with the teen-led plot and theme of a James Patterson MAXIMUM RIDE novel? The new Young Adult genre attempt by the aforementioned Reichs (with some success and some downfall).<br/><br/>Going into the novel, I was not expecting anything Reichs-ian (read: detailed forensic anthropology leading to the solution of one or many murders) and did expect to get a little Theodore Boone (Grisham's YA character) meets Maximum Ride. I got that, with</span>
  <span id="freeText6320412401876384851" style="display:none">What do you get when you mix the forensic description of Kathy Reichs with the teen-led plot and theme of a James Patterson MAXIMUM RIDE novel? The new Young Adult genre attempt by the aforementioned Reichs (with some success and some downfall).<br /><br />Going into the novel, I was not expecting anything Reichs-ian (read: detailed forensic anthropology leading to the solution of one or many murders) and did expect to get a little Theodore Boone (Grisham's YA character) meets Maximum Ride. I got that, with a little pizzazz in between. Reichs does handle the story well, watering the tale down to something YAs might feel (the pressures of school, dating, etc), but also the off-the-wall storyline of teen VIRALS (hence the book title). A medical mystery, a set of bones, how the stories do eventually merge together, and the teeny bopper feelings that surrounds it all.<br /><br />One note that Reichs may find interesting (and libraries, when cataloguing the book genre) is that while the genre is YOUNG ADULT, usually these books are geared to teenagers, to bait them into reading something more interesting than UNDERGROUND TO CANADA, TO KILL A MOCKINGBIRD, or HAMLET (pardons to Barbata Smucker, Harper Lee, and The Bard). It is NOT usually geared to young 18-22 year olds. I say this because the book is peppered with (WARNING, less than churchy language to follow) 'slut', 'bullshit', and 'bastard'. While I have no problem with it, might not be the place in this genre. While I know Patterson's use of 'darn', 'frig', etc does annoy me, it is proper for the aimed age category. Just saying.<br /><br />Yah, I will read SEIZURE, as I am a huge Reichs fan (have FLASH AND BONES already started) and will see how it fares.<br /><br />Kudos Madam Reichs!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6320412401876384851" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1594311248490180757">starting my cleaning out the closet 2019 challenge, this book has been on it since 2012!<br/><br/>1.5 stars<br/>I did not enjoy this. I took breaks from reading to clean out my pantry. yeah, it was like that. It wasn't all bad, there were some things I appreciated about it, but overall, I was like <br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1546709140ra/26864120.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Now, I'm all for super bright kids, for the cliche group where one is the science nerd and one is the tech nerd and one is afraid of everything but goes along anyway (he was actually my favorite!) so I can deal, but </span>
  <span id="freeText1594311248490180757" style="display:none">starting my cleaning out the closet 2019 challenge, this book has been on it since 2012!<br><br>1.5 stars<br>I did not enjoy this. Also, there's a trio of mean girls. But we're told they're just jealous. There's a popular boy who looks at her and winks. <b>What could it all mean?!</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1546709140ra/26864119.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Because of course in the middle of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ all the felonies my friends and I are committing, the times we were shot at or found that experimented on wolfpup, or that dead body we found, I mean, let's forget the vomiting, diarrhea, blackouts, fatigue, I mean <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> you MUST got to that dance and swoon when a cute boy notices you! gag me. <br>Anyhoo, part of me feels like maybe I'm too old, though I've got to say, these teens did not act like teens, and it's hard to imagine any teen actually caring about some of the other details. <div id="review_314507756" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/314507756" />
    <a title="Lynne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2294830-lynne"><img alt="Lynne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1389008986p2/2294830.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/314507756?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lynne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lynne" href="/user/show/2294830-lynne">Lynne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">nobody. The teens I know would laugh at the slang anyway</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Lynne by: </span>
      found it in an online library
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2294830-lynne?shelf=ya-fantasy-sci-fi">ya-fantasy-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2294830-lynne?shelf=whyyyyy">whyyyyy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer314507756" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13470981652526629937">As a late-to-the-party fan of the TV series, "Bones," I thought I'd give Kathy Reichs's books a try. Unfortunately, her first foray into YA has not made a good first impression on me. <br/><br/>As regards YA lit, I have some pet peeves, and Reichs seems to have touched every nerve. I hate it when authors think kids are stupid or that they don't deserve thoughtfully-drawn plots and carefully-crafted prose. Reichs, who probably has more money than God, with several bestsellers and a hit TV series under her </span>
  <span id="freeText13470981652526629937" style="display:none">As a late-to-the-party fan of the TV series, "Bones," I thought I'd give Kathy Reichs's books a try. Unfortunately, her first foray into YA has not made a good first impression on me. <br /><br />As regards YA lit, I have some pet peeves, and Reichs seems to have touched every nerve. I hate it when authors think kids are stupid or that they don't deserve thoughtfully-drawn plots and carefully-crafted prose. Reichs, who probably has more money than God, with several bestsellers and a hit TV series under her belt, just had to try to cash in on the lucrative and already-too-glutted-with-mediocrity teen market. She gives her teenaged audience cartoonish dialogue, forced stupidity to advance the plot, and flat, contrived characters. Tory Brennan will not go down in the annals of YA lit as a badass female role model for young women. There's a line between impetuous and thoughtless, between brave and foolhardy, and Tory crosses it too many times. There's no ebb and flow in the plot, just a big, drenching tsunami from a writer trying too hard.<br /><br />I have a copy of her <i>Deja Dead</i> that we found on Paperback Swap and will give that a try to see if she's any better at adult fiction, but one member of my family has already abandoned it, with the comment: "This is an author who's had an interesting life. Too bad she couldn't make me give a crap." </span>
  <a data-text-id="13470981652526629937" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_868271870" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/868271870" />
    <a title="Noella" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2439858-noella"><img alt="Noella" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435333948p2/2439858.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/868271870?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Noella" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Noella" href="/user/show/2439858-noella">Noella</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2439858-noella?shelf=own-physical-copy">own-physical-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2439858-noella?shelf=oct-15-family-fortunes">oct-15-family-fortunes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer868271870" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1646773064184978004">This is the first book I've read written by Kathy Reichs. The summary drew me in with the paranormal twist and since the main character was related to Temperance Brennan, I thought this would be a good introduction to the author's works. The writing style did not really engage me at first but the story line seemed promising. <br/><br/>The story follows 14 year old Tory Brennan and her friends as they are exposed to a virus and are put in great danger when they uncover a murder case. First of all, I though</span>
  <span id="freeText1646773064184978004" style="display:none">This is the first book I've read written by Kathy Reichs. The summary drew me in with the paranormal twist and since the main character was related to Temperance Brennan, I thought this would be a good introduction to the author's works. The writing style did not really engage me at first but the story line seemed promising. <br /><br />The story follows 14 year old Tory Brennan and her friends as they are exposed to a virus and are put in great danger when they uncover a murder case. First of all, I thought it was noticeable how Tory didn't really act like a teenager. She'd have these moments where she would be immature but then other times she'd switch to a different person and become an expert on science/anatomy (supposedly from reading her aunt's books). I really had to suspend my belief when Tory and her friends were able to repeatedly get past high security, understand how to pick locks and identify bones with no prior experience, to name a few things. Nevertheless, the book was enjoyable once I got past that (and the stereotypical high school drama. Think unattainable popular guy and mean girls in a group of three.) The twist at the end was quite extreme it took me by surprise. I liked how there were layers of mystery to peel away before we discovered the motives of the murderer and how events and other people fitted around them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1646773064184978004" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('FrbKoRT7gaFN4M4+0d8JwBOE5x6HgTjBVPBp8uKP3BsskKNzr6VIyerLel8mKgMfxdsA1kkMtqYPji9DL8wugQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hZ9t59HNRNlVBPvMYaXVr0Akkrl9Xxun0YJfeSy4DhG/uQQ1apONsfIvT62WUN9wlnt1cbPSlcCK/BnI4fv8iw==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer7543036993703174598">Kathy Reichs is a forensic anthropologist for the Office of the Chief Medical Examiner, State of North Carolina, and for the Laboratoire des Sciences Judiciaires et de Médecine Légale for the province of Quebec. She is one of only fifty forensic anthropologists certified by the American Board of Forensic Anthropology and is on the Board of Directors of the American Academy of Forensic Sciences. A </span>
  <span id="freeText7543036993703174598" style="display:none">Kathy Reichs is a forensic anthropologist for the Office of the Chief Medical Examiner, State of North Carolina, and for the Laboratoire des Sciences Judiciaires et de Médecine Légale for the province of Quebec. She is one of only fifty forensic anthropologists certified by the American Board of Forensic Anthropology and is on the Board of Directors of the American Academy of Forensic Sciences. A professor of anthropology at The University of North Carolina at Charlotte, Dr. Reichs is a native of Chicago, where she received her Ph.D. at Northwestern. She now divides her time between Charlotte and Montreal and is a frequent expert witness in criminal trials.<br /><br /><b>Awards:</b><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/award/show/1066-arthur-ellis-award" rel="nofollow noopener">Arthur Ellis Award</a><br />◊ Best First Novel (1998): Deja Dead</span>
